First Proof for the Pre-Eternity of Time
The author presents a rational proof for the pre-eternity of time via a trilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that establishes the pre-eternity of time (qidam al-mudda) as a necessary consequence of the Creator's precedence over the world.

Core Idea
The Creator's infinite precedence over the world proves time is eternal.

This lesson presents the first proof for the pre-eternity of time, a foundational argument in Islamic theology. The author constructs a logical trilemma to demonstrate that time must be eternal. By considering the possible relationships between the Creator and the world, only one conclusion remains: that the duration of precedence is infinite, and thus time is pre-eternal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the three possibilities presented: together, infinite posterior, finite posterior.
The passage ends mid-objection, but the core argument is complete.
2
Identify the logical structure
Recognize this as a trilemma: three options, two are eliminated, and the third is established.
3
Understand the refutation of the first possibility
Why can the Creator and world not be together? Because it would imply either both eternal or both originated, which contradicts the Creator's nature.
The author argues both subcases are impossible.
4
Understand the refutation of the second possibility
Why can precedence not be by a finite duration? Because whatever precedes an originated thing by a finite duration must itself be originated, leading to the Creator's origination.
This is impossible for the Creator.
5
Grasp the conclusion and reformulation
The only remaining possibility is infinite precedence, which necessitates that the duration itself is eternal. The author then offers a version without mentioning the world's pre-eternity.
The objection is cut off, but the main argument stands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المجوه المستنبطة في هذا الباب من الزمان
فالحجة الأولى : أن يقال : البارىء والعالم. إما أن يقال : إنهما وجدا معاً ، أو يقال : العالم متأخر عن البارىء بمدة غير متناهية ، أو متأخر عنه بمدة متناهية . والقسم الأول والثاني باطل (۱) فتعين الثالث
وإنما قلنا : إن القسم الأول باطل ، إذ لو كان البارىء والعالم معاً ، لزم أن يكونا معاً قديمين (٢) أو يكونا معاً محدثين . وإنما قلنا : إن القسم الثاني باطل . لأن المتقدم على المحدث بمدة متناهية يكون محدثاً . فيلزم حدوث البارىء . فبقي الثالث وهو أن يقال : البارىء متقدم على العالم بمدة غير متناهية ، فهذا يوجب القول بأن تلك المدة التي بسببها تقدم البارىء على العالم تقدماً لا نهاية له تكون قديمة ، فهذا يوجب قدم المدة
ويمكن ذكر هذا الكلام في تقرير قدم المدة، بحيث لا يحتاج فيه إلى ذكر قدم العالم. فيقال : لا شك أن البارىء متقدم على الحوادث الحادثة في هذا اليوم ، فإما أن يكون تقدمه عليها بمدة متناهية، أو بمدة غير متناهية . والأول يوجب حدوث البارىء ، والثاني يوجب قدم المدة . فإن قيل : هذا بناء على أن تقدم البارىء على العالم ، أو على هذا الحادث المعين بمدة، حتى يقال بعد
The conclusions extracted in this chapter concerning time. The first proof: It is said: the Creator (al-Bari') and the world (al-'alam). Either it is said that they both existed together, or it is said that the world is posterior to the Creator by an infinite duration, or posterior to Him by a finite duration. The first and second divisions are false (1), so the third is established. We say: the first division is false because if the Creator and the world were together, it would necessitate that they both be eternal (2) or that they both be originated. We say: the second division is false because that which precedes an originated thing by a finite duration is itself originated. So the origination (huduth) of the Creator would follow. So the third remains, which is that it is said: the Creator precedes the world by an infinite duration. This necessitates the statement that that duration, by which the Creator precedes the world with a precedence that has no end, is eternal (qadima); this necessitates the pre-eternity of time (qidam al-mudda). And this statement can be mentioned in establishing the pre-eternity of time in such a way that it does not need to mention the pre-eternity of the world. So it is said: there is no doubt that the Creator precedes the events occurring this day. Either His precedence over them is by a finite duration or by an infinite duration. The first necessitates the origination of the Creator, and the second necessitates the pre-eternity of time. Then it is said: this is based on the fact that the precedence of the Creator over the world, or over this specific event, is by a duration, so that it is said after...
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof (al-hujja al-ula) for the pre-eternity of time (qidam al-mudda). It is a rational demonstration structured as a trilemma. The author first states three possibilities regarding the relationship between the Creator (al-Bari') and the world (al-'alam): (1) they both exist together, (2) the world is posterior by an infinite duration, or (3) the world is posterior by a finite duration. He immediately declares the first and second false, establishing the third. He then explains the falsity of each: if they were together, both would have to be either eternal or originated—both impossible for the Creator; if the world is posterior by a finite duration, then that which precedes an originated thing by a finite duration is itself originated, implying the Creator's origination—also impossible. Thus the only remaining possibility is that the Creator precedes the world by an infinite duration. This infinite duration must be eternal (qadima), leading to the conclusion that time (al-mudda) is pre-eternal. The author then offers a reformulation of the argument that avoids any mention of the world's pre-eternity, focusing instead on a specific contemporary event: the Creator's precedence over today's events must be either by a finite or infinite duration; the finite would imply the Creator's origination, so it must be infinite, again proving time's pre-eternity. The passage ends with an objection (fa-in qila) that challenges the assumption that the precedence is by a duration, but the objection is cut off mid-sentence. The argument as presented is a classic kalam demonstration of the eternal nature of time as a necessary concomitant of the Creator's preexistence.

Key Terms
البارىء
العالم
المدة
قدم المدة
حدوث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This proof demonstrates that the world itself is eternal.
Correction: The proof only establishes the pre-eternity of time (al-mudda), not the world (al-‘alam). The world’s origination is not negated; time is argued to be an eternal concomitant of the Creator’s precedence.

Checkpoint
According to the first proof, which of the three possibilities regarding the Creator and the world is deemed true?
A) They exist together.
B) The world is posterior by a finite duration.
C) The world is posterior by an infinite duration.
D) None of the above.

Key Takeaway
The pre-eternity of time is a necessary consequence of the Creator's infinite precedence over the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Creator's precedence over every event today is infinite, then every moment of your life is connected to an endless past. How does that change the way you view the weight of your choices—does it make them more significant or less? What does it mean to live each moment before the eyes of the One who has always existed?
?
The proof shows that time itself is pre-eternal, a measure of the Creator's precedence. Yet you experience time as something that flows and ends. In what ways have you been living as if time is merely a resource for your own plans, rather than a sign of the Eternal? How can you make your use of time today a direct acknowledgment of the Creator who precedes it?
?
This argument eliminates the possibility that the Creator originated—it is impossible for the Eternal to have a beginning. If you truly internalize that the One you worship is absolutely prior to all things, what does that imply about your own sense of self-importance? How can you cultivate a deeper humility by reflecting on the infinite precedence of the Creator over every event, including your own existence?

First Proof: Priority of Yesterday Not by Duration
First proof using analogy of yesterday and today.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the analogy of yesterday's priority to today demonstrates that the Creator's priority cannot be temporal.

Core Idea
If yesterday's priority to today is not by time, then neither is the Creator's.

The author begins refuting the idea that the Creator's priority to the world is measured by time. The first proof uses a simple everyday example: the relationship between yesterday and today. This argument shows that temporal priority leads to an infinite regress, so the only coherent alternative is a non-temporal priority.

Guided Path
1
Read the first proof text
Read the Arabic passage for the first proof and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if...then...'
2
Identify the analogy
The proof uses an analogy between 'yesterday's priority to today' and 'the Creator's priority to the world'. Understand how the analogy works.
The key is that we intuitively understand yesterday's priority is not by a duration.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
If yesterday's priority were by a duration, that duration would need another duration, leading to an infinite chain. This is impossible, so the initial assumption is false.
This is a reduction ad absurdum.
4
Apply the conclusion
Since the priority of yesterday is not temporal, we can apply the same reasoning to the Creator's priority, concluding it is also not temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : هذا بناء على أن تقدم البارى على العالم أو على هذا الحادث المعين بمدة حتى يقال بعد ذلك : إن تلك المدة إما أن تكون متناهية أو غير متناهية . وذلك باطل فإنه لا يجوز أن يقال : البارى تعالى متقدم على العالم بالمدة . والدليل على بطلان هذا القول وجوه : الأول : إن تقدم الأمس على اليوم ليس بالزمان والمدة . وإلا لزم وقوع المدة في مدة أخرى إلى ما لا نهاية له . وإذا عقل أن يكون تقدم الأمس على اليوم لا بالمدة فلم لا يعقل أن يكون تقدم وجود البارى على وجود العالم لا بالمدة ؟ الثاني : إن المدة عبارة عن آنات منقضية سيالة فكل واحد من تلك الآنات قد كان معدوماً ثم صار موجوداً وكل ما كان كذلك فهو ممكن وكل ممكن فله محدث فلمجموع الزمان محدث هو فاعل مختار والفاعل المختار لا بد وأن يكون متقدماً على مفعوله فيكون البارى متقدماً في الوجود على وجود المدة والزمان وتقدمه على المدة يمتنع أن يكون بالمدة وإلا لزم كون المدة موجودة حال كونها معدومة وذلك محال الثالث : إن ماهية المدة متعلقة بالتغير من حال إلى حال والتغير ماهيته تقتضي المسبوقية بالحال المتنقل عنه فماهية المدة تقتضي المسبوقية بالغير وماهية الأزل تنافي المسبوقية بالغير والجمع بينهما محال الرابع : إن الآن الحاضر ما كان موجوداً قبل حضوره وسيعدم بعد دخوله في الوجود وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه ممكن لذاته وكل ممكن لذاته فإنه لا يمتنع أن يفنى ويوجد مثله عقيبه
Then it is said: This is based on the fact that the priority of the Creator to the world or to this specific event is by a duration, so that it is then said: that duration is either finite or infinite. But that is false, for it is not permissible to say: the Creator, exalted is He, is prior to the world by time. The proof of the falsity of this statement has aspects: First: The priority of yesterday to today is not by time and duration; otherwise it would necessitate the occurrence of duration within another duration ad infinitum. And if it is understood that the priority of yesterday to today is not by duration, why should it not be understood that the priority of the existence of the Creator to the existence of the world is not by duration? Second: Duration consists of passing, flowing instants. Each of those instants was non-existent then became existent. Everything that is like that is possible (mumkin), and every possible thing has an originator (muhdith). So the totality of time has an originator, who is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar). The free agent must be prior to its effect, so the Creator is prior in existence to the existence of duration and time. His priority to duration cannot be by duration, otherwise it would necessitate that duration exists while it is non-existent—and that is impossible. Third: The essence of duration (mahiyya al-midda) is connected to change from one state to another. Change in its essence necessitates being preceded by the state from which it changes. Thus the essence of duration necessitates being preceded by another, while the essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) negates being preceded by another. Combining them is impossible. Fourth: The present instant was not existent before its presence and will cease to exist after it enters into existence. Everything that is like that is possible in itself (mumkin li dhatihi). Every possible in itself does not preclude that it could perish and something like it come into existence after it.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The objection states that the previous argument (from the first lesson) assumes the Creator's priority to the world is by a duration, which is then judged as finite or infinite. But the objector claims that this assumption is false: it is not permissible to say the Creator is prior to the world by time (bi al-midda). The author then provides four proofs (وجوه) to demonstrate the falsity of temporal priority.

First proof: The priority of yesterday to today is not by time; if it were, time would be contained within another time ad infinitum. Since we understand that yesterday's priority is not temporal, we should similarly understand the Creator's priority as non-temporal.

Second proof: Duration consists of passing instants, each of which was non-existent then became existent—so each is possible (mumkin) and thus has an originator. Therefore the whole of time has an originator, who is a free agent. A free agent must be prior to its effect, so the Creator is prior to time. This priority cannot itself be temporal, for that would require time to exist while non-existent, an absurdity.

Third proof: The essence of duration is tied to change (taghayyur), and change requires being preceded by the state one changes from. Thus duration's essence demands being preceded by something else. The essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) negates being preceded. Hence duration and pre-eternity cannot coexist in the same thing.

Fourth proof: The present instant is preceded by non-existence and followed by non-existence, so it is possible in itself (mumkin li dhatihi). A possible thing can perish and be replaced by another. This shows that the present instant is not eternal.

Together, these four proofs establish that the Creator's priority to the world is not temporal, thus rejecting the objection and supporting the conclusion that duration is not a necessary intermediary between the Creator and creation.

Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum)
مدة (midda)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that because the Creator is prior, there must be a time before creation.
Correction: This proof shows that priority does not require time; even everyday priority (yesterday before today) is not temporal.

Checkpoint
What does the first proof argue would happen if the priority of yesterday to today were by duration?
A) Yesterday and today would be simultaneous.
B) Duration would be contained within another duration ad infinitum.
C) The Creator would not be prior to the world.
D) There would be no time at all.

Key Takeaway
The priority of yesterday to today shows that a non-temporal priority is conceivable and applies to the Creator.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you unconsciously believe that 'more time' equals 'greater priority'? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what would it mean for you to prioritize Allah without measuring it by minutes?
?
If the priority of yesterday to today is not by duration, then your relationship with Allah is not about how long you've been Muslim or how many years you've prayed. So what is the real measure of your priority to Him? Will you examine your heart today for what truly comes first, even if your schedule says otherwise?
?
The proof shows that cause can precede effect without time. Are you using lack of time as an excuse to delay obedience to Allah? What is one action you can take today that gives Allah priority not because you have extra time, but because He deserves the first place in your intention and action?

Second Proof: Duration as Possible Instants
Second proof analyzing the composition of duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the composition of time from possible instants leads to the necessity of a free agent prior to time.

Core Idea
Time is made of possible instants, so time itself has a cause prior to it.

The second proof focuses on the nature of duration itself. Duration is composed of passing instants, each of which was non-existent and then came into existence. This demonstrates that each instant is possible, hence the whole of time is possible and requires an originator. This originator must be a free agent, and such an agent must be prior to its effect—not temporally, but ontologically.

Guided Path
1
Read the second proof text
Read the Arabic and translation. Identify the main components: definition of duration, status of instants, conclusion.
2
Analyze the argument chain
Follow the logical sequence: duration = passing instants → each instant was non-existent then exists → possible → each possible has a cause → sum of time has cause = free agent → free agent prior to effect → hence Creator prior to time.
Use the guided breakdown below.
3
Understand the impossibility of temporal priority for the Creator
If the Creator were prior to time by time, that time would exist while the Creator is prior, but then the Creator would be before time, meaning time exists alongside the Creator? The proof shows this leads to absurdity.
The conclusion is that the Creator's priority cannot be temporal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : هذا بناء على أن تقدم البارى على العالم أو على هذا الحادث المعين بمدة حتى يقال بعد ذلك : إن تلك المدة إما أن تكون متناهية أو غير متناهية . وذلك باطل فإنه لا يجوز أن يقال : البارى تعالى متقدم على العالم بالمدة . والدليل على بطلان هذا القول وجوه : الأول : إن تقدم الأمس على اليوم ليس بالزمان والمدة . وإلا لزم وقوع المدة في مدة أخرى إلى ما لا نهاية له . وإذا عقل أن يكون تقدم الأمس على اليوم لا بالمدة فلم لا يعقل أن يكون تقدم وجود البارى على وجود العالم لا بالمدة ؟ الثاني : إن المدة عبارة عن آنات منقضية سيالة فكل واحد من تلك الآنات قد كان معدوماً ثم صار موجوداً وكل ما كان كذلك فهو ممكن وكل ممكن فله محدث فلمجموع الزمان محدث هو فاعل مختار والفاعل المختار لا بد وأن يكون متقدماً على مفعوله فيكون البارى متقدماً في الوجود على وجود المدة والزمان وتقدمه على المدة يمتنع أن يكون بالمدة وإلا لزم كون المدة موجودة حال كونها معدومة وذلك محال الثالث : إن ماهية المدة متعلقة بالتغير من حال إلى حال والتغير ماهيته تقتضي المسبوقية بالحال المتنقل عنه فماهية المدة تقتضي المسبوقية بالغير وماهية الأزل تنافي المسبوقية بالغير والجمع بينهما محال الرابع : إن الآن الحاضر ما كان موجوداً قبل حضوره وسيعدم بعد دخوله في الوجود وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه ممكن لذاته وكل ممكن لذاته فإنه لا يمتنع أن يفنى ويوجد مثله عقيبه
Then it is said: This is based on the fact that the priority of the Creator to the world or to this specific event is by a duration, so that it is then said: that duration is either finite or infinite. But that is false, for it is not permissible to say: the Creator, exalted is He, is prior to the world by time. The proof of the falsity of this statement has aspects: First: The priority of yesterday to today is not by time and duration; otherwise it would necessitate the occurrence of duration within another duration ad infinitum. And if it is understood that the priority of yesterday to today is not by duration, why should it not be understood that the priority of the existence of the Creator to the existence of the world is not by duration? Second: Duration consists of passing, flowing instants. Each of those instants was non-existent then became existent. Everything that is like that is possible (mumkin), and every possible thing has an originator (muhdith). So the totality of time has an originator, who is a free agent (fa'il mukhtar). The free agent must be prior to its effect, so the Creator is prior in existence to the existence of duration and time. His priority to duration cannot be by duration, otherwise it would necessitate that duration exists while it is non-existent—and that is impossible. Third: The essence of duration (mahiyya al-midda) is connected to change from one state to another. Change in its essence necessitates being preceded by the state from which it changes. Thus the essence of duration necessitates being preceded by another, while the essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) negates being preceded by another. Combining them is impossible. Fourth: The present instant was not existent before its presence and will cease to exist after it enters into existence. Everything that is like that is possible in itself (mumkin li dhatihi). Every possible in itself does not preclude that it could perish and something like it come into existence after it.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The objection states that the previous argument (from the first lesson) assumes the Creator's priority to the world is by a duration, which is then judged as finite or infinite. But the objector claims that this assumption is false: it is not permissible to say the Creator is prior to the world by time (bi al-midda). The author then provides four proofs (وجوه) to demonstrate the falsity of temporal priority.

First proof: The priority of yesterday to today is not by time; if it were, time would be contained within another time ad infinitum. Since we understand that yesterday's priority is not temporal, we should similarly understand the Creator's priority as non-temporal.

Second proof: Duration consists of passing instants, each of which was non-existent then became existent—so each is possible (mumkin) and thus has an originator. Therefore the whole of time has an originator, who is a free agent. A free agent must be prior to its effect, so the Creator is prior to time. This priority cannot itself be temporal, for that would require time to exist while non-existent, an absurdity.

Third proof: The essence of duration is tied to change (taghayyur), and change requires being preceded by the state one changes from. Thus duration's essence demands being preceded by something else. The essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) negates being preceded. Hence duration and pre-eternity cannot coexist in the same thing.

Fourth proof: The present instant is preceded by non-existence and followed by non-existence, so it is possible in itself (mumkin li dhatihi). A possible thing can perish and be replaced by another. This shows that the present instant is not eternal.

Together, these four proofs establish that the Creator's priority to the world is not temporal, thus rejecting the objection and supporting the conclusion that duration is not a necessary intermediary between the Creator and creation.

Key Terms
مدة (midda)
آنات (anāt)
ممكن (mumkin)
محدث (muhdith)
فاعل مختار (fa'il mukhtar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that time is eternal and uncreated.
Correction: This proof demonstrates that time is composed of contingent instants, so time itself is created and has a Creator.

Checkpoint
What is the status of each instant of time according to the second proof?
A) Eternal and uncreated.
B) Non-existent then existent, hence possible.
C) Necessary in itself.
D) Part of the Creator's essence.

Key Takeaway
Time is composed of contingent instants, so time itself must have a Creator who is prior to time in a non-temporal sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You exist within time, and every moment of your life is a passing instant. Since time itself is contingent and has a Creator outside it, are you living as if your moments are gifts from the One who created time, or do you act as if your time is your own? What would change if you truly believed that your next breath is given to you by the Creator of time?
?
The proof shows that the Creator is prior to time, not in a temporal way. Have you ever considered that your relationship with Allah is not limited to the time you spend in worship? Since He is beyond time, how does that affect your understanding of His constant awareness of you, even when you forget Him?
?
If every instant of your life is possible and could have been non-existent, why do you still feel secure in your plans? Does your heart truly rely on the Originator of time, or have you been lulled into thinking that your future is guaranteed? What is one thing you can do today to acknowledge your utter dependence on the Creator of every passing moment?

Third Proof: Essence of Duration Contradicts Pre-Eternity
Third proof on the incompatibility of duration and pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the essence of duration (change) is incompatible with the essence of pre-eternity (al-azal).

Core Idea
Duration's essence requires change and being preceded; pre-eternity negates this.

The third proof takes a more metaphysical approach by analyzing the very essence (mahiyya) of duration. Duration is inherently linked to change from one state to another. Change by its nature presupposes a prior state from which the change occurs. Therefore, duration requires being preceded by something else. In contrast, the essence of pre-eternity (al-azal) is defined by the absence of any precedence. Since these two essences are contradictory, duration cannot be attributed to the pre-eternal Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the third proof text
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the terms: ماهية المدة, التغير, أزل.
2
Understand the essence of duration
Duration is defined by change (taghayyur). Change requires a starting point and a prior state.
This is a core metaphysical concept.
3
Understand the essence of pre-eternity
Pre-eternity (al-azal) means 'no beginning' and 'not preceded by anything'.
4
Recognize the contradiction
If duration were attributed to the Creator, then the Creator would have a nature that is both preceded (by change) and not preceded (by pre-eternity), which is impossible.
Hence, the Creator's priority is not temporal.

Fourth Proof: The Present Instant is Possible
Fourth proof examining the contingency of the present instant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the transient nature of the present moment proves that time is not eternal.

Core Idea
The present instant is possible and can be replaced, so time is created.

The fourth proof examines the present moment (الآن الحاضر). The present instant was not existent before it arrived, and it will cease to exist after passing. This temporal boundedness indicates that the instant is contingent (possible in itself). If it were necessary, it would be eternal. Since it is possible, it can cease to exist and be replaced by another similar instant. This shows that time is not a necessary entity but a sequence of contingent moments, pointing to a Creator who brings them into existence and causes them to perish.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth proof text
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the description of the present instant.
2
Identify the properties of the present instant
The present instant was not existent before and will cease after. That makes it possible (mumkin li dhatihi).
3
Understand the implication of possibility
A possible thing can perish and be replaced by another. This shows the instant is not eternal.
This undermines the idea that time is uncreated.
4
Connect to the overall argument
If the present instant is possible, then time as a whole is possible and requires a creator who is not temporal.

?
This instant you are reading these words will soon perish. What is one action you can take right now—not later—that will have eternal weight? Do it before the moment is lost.

Answer to the objection that God cannot be temporal
Sanusi reiterates the earlier proof that God's priority is by duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a seemingly strong objection against God's temporal priority is answered simply by referring back to the established proof that God is eternal and the world is originated.

Core Idea
The objection's force dissolves when the original proof is reaffirmed.

This lesson addresses a specific objection raised against the doctrine of God's priority over the world. The objector claims that God cannot be temporal (zamanī). However, as Sanusi points out, the earlier argument that God is eternal (azalī) and the world is originated (hadith) already entails that God is prior by duration. Thus, the objection is not a new difficulty but a misunderstanding of the proof's implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer

These terms are central to the proof.
3
Analyze the answer's logic
Observe that the answer does not introduce new arguments. It simply restates the logical implication: if God is eternal and the world is originated, then God must be prior by duration. The objection is thereby answered.
The strength of the answer lies in its reliance on an earlier established proof.

Response to the Sixth Objection: Creator's Priority by Duration
Author rebuts the sixth objection about Creator's temporality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the objection that the Creator cannot be temporal by demonstrating that His pre-eternity and the world's temporality logically require a priority in duration.

Core Idea
God's pre-eternity and the world's temporality entail a time-based priority.

In this brief passage, the author tackles a sixth objection: that the Creator cannot be temporal in any sense. He counters by referencing a previously established point: since the Creator is pre-eternal and the world is temporal, it necessarily follows that the Creator is prior to the world by a duration. This duration implies a temporal interval between the Creator's existence and the world's creation, without attributing temporality to the Creator's essence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation

The phrase 'والله أعلم' is a standard closing.
2

The objection says the Creator cannot be temporal (زمانياً). The response argues from two premises: Creator is pre-eternal (أزلياً), world is temporal (حادثاً). The conclusion: Creator is prior by a duration (متقدماً بالمدة).
3
Understand the logical implication
The argument is a conditional: if the Creator is pre-eternal and the world is temporal, then His priority must involve a duration. This does not mean He is temporal in the sense of being originated; rather, it means there is a measurable temporal gap between His existence and the world's beginning.
Think about what 'duration' implies about the existence of time.
4

The Argument from the Agent's Will for the Eternity of Time
The author argues that God's will necessitates the eternity of time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the nature of God's will implies that time has no beginning.

Core Idea
An eternal will cannot delay its effect; therefore time must be eternal.

This passage presents a logical argument for the eternity of time. It examines two possibilities regarding God's intention to create time. In both cases, the argument concludes that time must be beginningless. Let's work through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the two divisions (qism) presented: one with a condition of specifying a time, and one without.
The argument begins mid-sentence; it builds on a prior supposition.
2
Analyze the first division
Identify why the first possibility (creation with a specified time) leads to an impossible infinite regress or a simultaneous infinite. Understand that the only coherent outcome is a sequence with no first moment.
This already points to time being beginningless.
3
Analyze the second division
Consider the second possibility: God intends to create time without specifying a particular moment. Since His intention is eternal and unconditional, the effect (time) must also be eternal—there is no reason for delay.
This directly concludes that time is eternal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفاعل . وعلى هذا التقدير، فنقول : إنه تعالى إما أن يقصد إحداث تلك المدة ، بشرط أن يخصص ذلك الإحداث بوقت معين ، أولاً بهذا الشرط . والأول محال . لأن الكلام في هذا الوقت، كالكلام في الأول ويلزم التسلسل ثم ذلك التسلسل إن وقع دفعة واحدة ، فهو محال . وإن وقع على أن يكون كل جزء منه مسبوقاً بغيره، لا إلى أول . فهو المطلوب . وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يقال : إنه تعالى قصد إحداث الوقت والزمان لا بشرط أن يوقع ذلك في زمان معين، بل قصد إحداث الوقت والزمان من غير هذا الشرط فعلى هذا التقدير وجب أن لا يتأخر وقوع الأثر عن ذلك القصد فلما كان القصد إلى تكوين المدة والزمان : أزلياً. وجب كون المدة والزمان : أزلياً . وهو المطلوب .
The agent. And upon this supposition, we say: He, exalted, either intends to bring about that duration, with the condition that He specifies that bringing about to a particular time, or not with this condition. The first is impossible because the discourse regarding this time is like the discourse regarding the first, and an infinite regress would follow. Then that regress, if it occurs all at once, is impossible. And if it occurs such that each part of it is preceded by another, without a first, then that is the desired conclusion. As for the second division: that it is said: He, exalted, intended to bring about time and duration, not with the condition that He bring that about in a particular time, but rather He intended to bring about time and duration without this condition. Upon this supposition, it is necessary that the occurrence of the effect not be delayed from that intent. So since the intent to generate duration and time was eternal, it is necessary that duration and time be eternal. And that is the desired conclusion.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage presents an argument for the eternity of time based on the nature of God's will. It is a logical division (qism) argument. The author considers two possibilities regarding God's intention to create duration (al-muddah) and time (al-zaman). First, if God intends to create it but specifies a particular moment for its creation, that leads to an infinite regress or an impossible simultaneous creation of infinite moments. The only coherent scenario is that each moment is preceded by another without a first, meaning time is eternal. Second, if God intends to create time without stipulating a particular moment, then since His intention is eternal, the effect (time) must also be eternal, as there is no reason for delay. Both divisions lead to the conclusion that time has no beginning. The argument relies on the principle that an eternal will necessitates an eternal effect unless there is a specific condition preventing it.

Key Terms
المدة
الزمان
القصد
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If time is eternal, then it is not created by God.
Correction: The argument does not deny creation; it asserts that time is eternally created, i.e., God's eternal will continuously produces time without beginning.

Checkpoint
According to the second division of the argument, why must time be eternal?
A) Because God's intention is eternal and unconditional, so the effect must be immediate.
B) Because time is not a created thing.
C) Because the first division leads to a contradiction.
D) Because God cannot create time at a specific moment.

Key Takeaway
The argument from the agent's will demonstrates that time must be beginningless because an eternal will cannot produce a delayed effect and any attempt to specify a moment leads to infinite regress or immediate eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's will is immediately effective, why do you allow your own good intentions to lie dormant? What is the gap between your intention to obey and your action, and what does that reveal about your heart?
?
The argument shows that time itself depends on God's eternal will. Do you live as if time is your own possession, or do you recognize every moment as a loan from the Eternal? When you feel the pressure of fleeting time, do you turn to the One who is not bound by it?
?
If time had no beginning, then your life is not an isolated span but part of an eternal plan. What would change in your daily priorities if you truly believed that your actions are eternally significant before an eternal God?

The Seventh Proof: Pre-eternity and Perpetuity are Distinct
Sanusi argues that pre-eternity and perpetuity are distinct from each other and from God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi's seventh proof uses rational self-evidence to show that the concepts of pre-eternity (al-azal) and perpetuity (al-abad) are distinct from each other and from God's essence.

Core Idea
Past and future are not the same concept—even for God.

Sanusi now presents a proof that appeals to our basic rational intuition about time and existence. We naturally distinguish between 'was in pre-eternity' and 'will be in perpetuity'. This proof shows that these two temporal concepts are not only distinct from each other but also distinct from God's essence, and therefore they are real attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the logical flow: it begins with a statement, poses a question, and then argues.
The passage is a compact argument; try to identify the main claim.
2
Identify the two possibilities and the rejection
The proof starts by stating two possibilities: either the concepts are distinct or they are not. Sanusi immediately rejects the second possibility as invalid by intellectual self-evidence.
Look for the phrase 'باطل في بديهة العقل'.
3
Understand the evidence from self-evidence
Sanusi argues that if the concepts were not distinct, then saying 'He was in the past' and 'He will be in the future' would have the same meaning, which is false. The self-evident intellect judges them to be different.
He also uses the absurd example of swapping past and future.
4
Trace the conclusion about God's essence
Since the concepts are distinct and God's essence is one, each concept must be other than His essence. They are also distinct from the concept of the world's non-existence.
The proof ends by establishing that pre-eternity and perpetuity are 'something' (amr).
5
Reflect on the significance
This proof shows that temporal attributes are not identical to God's essence but are real distinctions in our understanding. It demonstrates how rational self-evidence can be used in kalam.
Consider how this connects to the broader topic of God's attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السابعة : لا شك أنه يصدق على ذات الله تعالى : أنه كان موجوداً في الأزل ، وأنه سيكون موجود في الأبد . فهل يتميز في حقه : مفهوم أنه كان موجوداً في الأزل ، عن مفهوم أنه موجود أو سيكون في لا يزال ، أو لا يتميز ؟ وهذا القسم الثاني : باطل في بديهة العقل ، لأنه إن لم يتميز أحد المفهومين عن الثاني ، لكان المفهوم من هذين الكلامين مفهوماً واحداً ، ولكان التعبير عنه بهذين اللفظين : مخض في العبارة. وبديهة العقل : حاكمة بأنه ليس كذلك . فإن المفهوم من قولنا : كان في الأزل : إشارة إلى الماضي . والمفهوم من قولنا : سيكون في لا يزال : إشارة إلى المستقبل . ولو غيرنا العبارة ، وقلنا : إنه كان في المستقبل ، وسيكون في الماضي ، فإن صريح العقل يشهد بفساده . فعلمنا : أن التغاير بين هذين المفهومين : حاصل في بديهة العقل . إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : إنه تعالى : محكوم عليه بالوجود . والحصول مع كل واحد من هذين المفهومين لكن واحداً من هذين المفهومين : غير محكوم عليه بالحصول ، مع المفهوم الآخر . وذلك يوجب كون كل واحد من هذين المفهومين مغايراً لذات الله تعالى. وأيضاً : فهما مغايران للمفهوم من كون العالم معدوماً ، فإن المفهوم من العدم ، يمكن تعقله مع الأزل تارة ، ومع الأبد أخرى . فيثبت : أن المفهوم من الأزل، وأن المفهوم من الأبد : أمر
The seventh proof: There is no doubt that it is true of the essence of God Most High that He was existent in pre-eternity (al-azal) and that He will be existent in perpetuity (al-abad). So, is the concept that He was existent in pre-eternity distinct in His regard from the concept that He is existent or will be in that which never ceases, or is it not distinct? This second option is invalid by the self-evidence of the intellect, because if the two concepts were not distinct, then the meaning of these two statements would be one meaning, and the expression by these two terms would be a mere verbal variation. But the self-evidence of the intellect judges that it is not so. For the meaning of our saying 'He was in pre-eternity' indicates the past, and the meaning of our saying 'He will be in that which never ceases' indicates the future. And if we change the expression and say 'He was in the future' and 'He will be in the past', then plain reason testifies to its falsehood. So we know that the distinction between these two concepts is established in the self-evidence of the intellect. If this is established, then we say: He Most High is judged to have existence (wujud). And His existence together with each of these two concepts is such that one of these concepts is not judged to be obtained together with the other concept. That necessitates that each of these two concepts is other than the essence of God Most High. Also, they are other than the concept of the world's non-existence, for the concept of non-existence can be conceived with pre-eternity sometimes and with perpetuity at other times. So it is established that the concept of pre-eternity and the concept of perpetuity are something (amr).
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh proof (al-hujja al-sabi'a) concerning the distinction between God's existence in pre-eternity (al-azal) and His existence in future eternity (al-abad). The argument begins with the obvious truth that we say both 'God was existent in pre-eternity' and 'God will be existent in perpetuity'. The proof asks whether the concept of 'was in pre-eternity' is distinct from 'will be in perpetuity'. The answer is that they are distinct by intellectual intuition (badiha al-'aql). If they were the same, then saying 'He was in the future' would be as valid, which is absurd. Therefore, these two concepts are distinct. Since God's essence is one, and these conceptual predicates differ, they must be distinct from His essence. Moreover, they are also distinct from the concept of the world's non-existence, because non-existence can be related to both pre-eternity and perpetuity. Thus, the concepts of pre-eternity and perpetuity are real things (amr). The proof aims to establish that temporal concepts (past and future) are not identical to God's essence but are attributed to it, implying that time has a reality distinct from God.

Key Terms
الحجة السابعة
الأزل
الأبد
الماضي
المستقبل
بديهة العقل
ذات الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's existence in the past and future is the same concept, so 'God was in pre-eternity' and 'God will be in perpetuity' mean the same thing.
Correction: The proof shows that these concepts are distinct by intellectual self-evidence: one refers to the past, the other to the future. They cannot be identical because swapping them yields absurdity.

Checkpoint
According to the seventh proof, why are the concepts of pre-eternity (al-azal) and perpetuity (al-abad) considered distinct from each other?
A) Because they are linguistic expressions with no real meaning.
B) Because the self-evident intellect judges them to be different, as one indicates the past and the other the future.
C) Because they are identical to God's essence.
D) Because they refer to the non-existence of the world.

Key Takeaway
The concepts of pre-eternity and perpetuity are distinct from each other and from God's essence, as proven by rational self-evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You regularly affirm that 'Allah was always there' and 'Allah will always be there' — but have you ever paused to realize that these two statements carry different meanings? If you had to explain this distinction to someone, could you do so from this proof?
?
The intellect clearly distinguishes past and future even in God's existence. If you ignore this distinction, do you reduce your understanding of God to a vague, timeless blur? What step will you take today to know Him through His distinct attributes as taught by the scholars?
?
Sanusi shows that pre-eternity and perpetuity are not merely verbal variations but real concepts distinct from God's essence. When you think of God's eternity, do you tend to treat 'pre-eternity' and 'perpetuity' as interchangeable? What does this proof demand of your belief about God's attributes?

The Tenth Proof: Possibility of Prior Worlds Implies Eternal Duration
Author argues that the possibility of worlds before this one entails an eternal pre-creative duration.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the possibility of multiple prior worlds of different durations leads to the conclusion that time (or duration) must be pre-eternal.

Core Idea
The very possibility of worlds of different lengths before this one proves that time has no beginning.

This is a key proof for the eternity of time in Islamic theology. The author presents a hypothetical scenario to demonstrate that time cannot have been created; rather, it must be a necessary backdrop for possibilities. This proof relies solely on rational argument, not scriptural authority, to establish that duration and time are eternal. By carefully analyzing what it would mean for a world to be possible before this one, the author shows that such possibilities imply a temporal sequence with no first moment.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation. Get a sense of the flow of the argument without analyzing deeply yet.
Notice the repeated phrase 'ثم نقول' which marks new steps in the proof.
2
Understand the initial assumption
The proof starts with a conditional: if the world is originated (muhdath), then consider a prior world that ends exactly at the start of this world after ten cycles.
The proof does not assert that such a world actually existed, only that it is conceivable and evaluates its possibility.
3
Eliminate the impossible branch
The author argues that if this prior world is not possible, it would require absurd changes in the world's essence or the Creator's power. Therefore, it must be possible.
This is a standard kalam reduction to absurdity (imtina').
4
Extend the reasoning to longer durations
The same reasoning applies to a world ending after twenty cycles. Both possibilities are established as valid.
Here the proof introduces two distinct possibilities of different lengths.
5
Derive the necessity of time
The two possibilities cannot coincide in time; one must begin before the other. This creates a sequence of possibilities, which is exactly what we mean by duration and time. Since this sequence has no first term, time must be eternal.
The conclusion is that time has no beginning (azali).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : لو كان العالم محدثاً ، فوجد عالم آخر قبل هذا العالم آخره إلى أول هذا العالم بعشرة أدوار ، إما أن يكون ممكناً، أو لا يكون ممكناً . والثاني يقتضي إما انتقال العالم من الإمتناع الذاتي إلى الإمكان الذاتي ، أو انتقال الخالق من العجز إلى القدرة . وكلاهما محالان . والأول يقتضي حصول الإمكان. ثم نقول : وكان أيضاً : يمكن خلق عالم آخر ، وينتهي إلى أول هذا العالم بعشرين دورة . والدليل عليه أيضاً : عين ما تقدم . ثم نقول : هذان الأمران المفروضان بتقدير وقوعهما إما أن يبتدئا معاً، وينتهيا معاً إلى أول هذا العالم، وإما أن يقال : إنها بتقدير وقوعهما يجب أن يكون ابتداء وجود أحدهما سابقاً على وجود الآخر. والأول باطل ، وإلا لزم كون الزائد مساوياً للناقص . وهو محال . والثاني يوجب القول بوجود المدة والزمان لأنه كان قد حصل قبل وجود العالم إمكان يتسع لعشرة دورات ، ولا يتسع لعشرين دورة . وإمكان آخر يتسع لعشرين دورة ، ولا يمتلىء بعشرة دورات . وكان هذا الإمكان الثاني متقرر الوجود قبل الإمكان الأول . ولا معنى للمدة والزمان إلا ذلك. وهذا يقتضي أن لا يكون للمدة والزمان : أول وهو المطلوب والله أعلم
The tenth proof: If the world were originated, and there existed another world before this world, its end [reaching] the beginning of this world in ten cycles (adwār) — either it is possible (mumkin) or it is not possible. The second [possibility] entails either a transition of the world from essential impossibility to essential possibility, or a transition of the Creator from incapacity to power. Both are impossible. The first [possibility] entails the attainment of possibility. Then we say: It would also be possible to create another world ending at the beginning of this world in twenty cycles. The proof for it is the same as before. Then we say: These two assumed matters, if they were to occur — either they begin together and end together at the beginning of this world, or it must be said that, given their occurrence, the beginning of the existence of one is prior to the existence of the other. The first is false, otherwise the greater would equal the lesser, which is impossible. The second necessitates affirming the existence of duration (al-mudda) and time (al-zamān), because before the existence of the world there had occurred a possibility (imkān) that accommodates ten cycles but not twenty cycles, and another possibility that accommodates twenty cycles and is not filled by ten cycles. And this second possibility was established in existence before the first possibility. Duration and time mean nothing other than that. And this necessitates that duration and time have no beginning, which is what is required. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a proof (ḥujja) for the eternity of time. The author presents a hypothetical: if the world is originated, consider the possibility of another world ending at the start of this world after ten cycles. This possibility is either possible or not. If not possible, it would require a change in the world's essential possibility or in the Creator's power, both absurd. So it is possible. Similarly, a world ending after twenty cycles is possible. Now, if both worlds were to occur simultaneously, they would need to end together at the same moment, but then the longer (twenty cycles) would equal the shorter (ten cycles), which is impossible. So one must begin before the other. The one beginning later is preceded by a possibility that accommodates ten cycles but not twenty, while the other is preceded by a capacity for twenty. This second possibility exists before the first, implying a temporal sequence of possibilities before any world exists. This sequence is nothing other than duration and time. Since this progression of possibilities has no first term, time has no beginning, i.e., it is eternal. The proof concludes that time (or duration) is pre-eternal.

Key Terms
الحجة العاشرة (al-ḥujja al-ʿāshira)
الإمكان (al-imkān)
المدة (al-mudda)
الزمان (al-zamān)
الأدوار (al-adwār)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the possibility of prior worlds is merely hypothetical and has no real implication.
Correction: The author uses this hypothetical to demonstrate that the very structure of possibility requires a temporal background that is eternal; the argument is not about actual prior worlds but about the logical conditions of possibility.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does the author draw from the possibility of worlds of different durations before this one?
A) That the world must be eternal.
B) That duration and time have no beginning.
C) That multiple worlds actually existed before this one.
D) That the Creator is powerful enough to create any number of worlds.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of prior worlds of different durations necessarily entails that time and duration have no beginning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time has no beginning, then Allah alone existed before all duration. Your life, by contrast, is a brief flicker within this infinite timeline. How does this truth reshape your perspective on what truly matters—your reputation, your wealth, or your standing with the Eternal? Will you let the weight of eternity drive you to examine your deeds today, or will you continue as if this moment will last forever?
?
The proof shows that possibilities before creation imply an endless past. Allah, the Creator, is not bound by time; He exists outside it. Yet you, a creature of time, will stand before Him for judgment. When you feel overwhelmed by the pressures of the present, does the reality of an eternal Allah who sees all times at once give you peace? Or does it unsettle you because it exposes the vanity of your earthly pursuits? Commit now to one action today that reflects that you truly believe in an eternal, all-seeing Lord.
?
Consider that the possibilities of different worlds existed before any world. Your own existence was once only a possibility in the knowledge of Allah. You could have been created in any time or place, but He chose to bring you into existence now, with this lesson before you. What does that say about His purpose for you? Are you living as if you were created by mere chance, or are you actively seeking the purpose for which He singled you out? What will you change starting today to align with His infinite wisdom?

Interval Increase Proves Time's Reality
Sanusi presents the eleventh proof for time's reality using comparatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the increasing interval from pre-eternity to successive events demonstrates that time is an objective reality, not a mere mental construct.

Core Idea
Increase and decrease in an interval prove it is an existing thing, not nothing.

This proof uses a simple observation: the distance from pre-eternity to later events keeps growing. Since only something that exists can change in size, the interval itself must be real. Sanusi is building a case for the reality of time as an entity, starting with comparative examples and then applying a logical principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof's comparative examples
Notice how the author compares intervals: from pre-eternity to first creation, to flood, to today. Each is larger than the previous.
The pattern makes the increase obvious.
2
Identify the key property
The interval admits increase and decrease. That property is the core of the argument.
3
Understand why non-existence cannot vary
Pure nothingness cannot be described as greater or lesser. So the interval must be an existing thing.
This is the logical foundation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر : وهو أن من الأزل إلى أول خلق العالم : أقل من الأزل إلى وقت الطوفان . وأيضاً : من الأزل إلى وقت الطوفان أقل من الأزل إلى هذا اليوم، الذي نحن فيه ، وكلما ازداد يوم، وحدث زمان ، صار من الأزل إلى ذلك الوقت : أزيد من الأزل ، إلى الوقت الذي كان قبله إذا ثبت هذا فنقول : ان من الأزل إلى الآن أمر يقبل الزيادة والنقصان وكل ما كان كذلك فهو موجود . لأن العدم المحض ، والسلب الصرف ، لا يمكن وصفه بكونه زائداً وناقصاً إذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : القابل لهذه الزياة
The eleventh proof: [It is] that from pre-eternity (al-azal) to the first creation of the world is less than from pre-eternity to the time of the flood. And also: from pre-eternity to the time of the flood is less than from pre-eternity to this day in which we are. And whenever a day increases and time occurs, the [interval] from pre-eternity to that time becomes greater than [the interval] from pre-eternity to the time before it. If this is established, we say: [the interval] from pre-eternity to now is something that admits increase and decrease. And everything that is like that is existent (mawjūd), because pure non-existence (al-ʿadam al-maḥḍ) and absolute negation (al-salb al-ṣirf) cannot be described as being greater or lesser. If this is established, we say: that which receives this increase…
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is the eleventh proof for the existence of time as a real entity. The author starts with comparative statements: the interval from pre-eternity to the first creation is less than to the flood, and that is less than to today. Every new day makes the interval longer. Thus, the 'from pre-eternity to now' is something that can increase and decrease. Only an existing thing can admit quantitative variation; pure nothingness cannot be described as greater or lesser. Therefore, that interval must be an existent reality. The argument is cut off but likely concludes that this existing interval is duration or time, which is therefore real and not a mere negation.

Key Terms
الأزل (al-azal)
الزيادة والنقصان (al-ziyāda wa al-nuqṣān)
العدم المحض (al-ʿadam al-maḥḍ)
السلب الصرف (al-salb al-ṣirf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is merely a mental abstraction or a relative measure with no objective existence.
Correction: The argument shows that time must have objective existence because the interval from pre-eternity to now can increase, which is a property of real things, not of nothingness.

Checkpoint
Why does the author argue that the interval from pre-eternity to now must be existent?
A) Because it can be measured in days.
B) Because it admits increase and decrease, which non-existence cannot.
C) Because the world is originated.
D) Because the Quran mentions time.

Key Takeaway
The interval from pre-eternity to now must be an existent reality because it can increase, unlike pure nothingness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the interval from pre-eternity to this very moment is an increasing, real thing that exists, then every second you live is adding to that reality. How will you ensure that the increase you cause from this day forward is something you would want to stand before Allah with?
?
You just learned that pure nothingness cannot be described as increasing or decreasing. Your own life is clearly increasing in time. Since you are not nothing, what does that mean for the purpose of your existence? What are you doing with the time that is being added right now?
?
The argument proves time is real because it receives increase. Your lifetime also receives increase. If you could stand at the end of your life and look back at the 'interval' from your birth to that moment, would it be a story of increasing obedience or increasing distance from your Lord? What will you change today?

The Tenth Proof: From Eternity to Pre-Eternity
He presents the tenth proof and argues that the eternal world must be pre-eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that, given the world's eternal existence (abadi), it must also be pre-eternal (azali), and the logical steps that lead from one to the other.

Core Idea
If the world is eternal, it cannot be receptive to non-existence, so it must be without beginning.

The philosophers have presented ten proofs that the world is eternal. Now they take the final step: from eternity to pre-eternity. This passage shows how they reason that an everlasting thing cannot have a beginning, because if it did, it would be capable of ceasing to exist—which contradicts its eternal nature. The argument is sharp and concise, using the impossibility of accepting non-existence as its pivot.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Try to follow the logic from the tenth proof through the conclusion that the world must be pre-eternal.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the tenth proof's premise
Notice that the proof starts with a property of the heavens: they do not accept straight motion. From this, the philosophers infer that they do not accept separation, generation, or corruption.
Straight motion is key—its absence means the heavens are changeless.
3
Trace the inference to pre-eternity
After stating that the world is eternal, the philosophers argue that it must be pre-eternal. They use a conditional chain: if not pre-eternal, then it was once non-existent; that would imply its essence can accept non-existence; that ability would persist, making it possible for the world to vanish later—which is impossible.
The argument turns on the 'receptivity to non-existence' concept.
4
Understand the conclusion
The chain ends with the impossibility of the world accepting non-existence, so it must be pre-eternal. This is the final step of the philosophers' case.
The argument does not prove the world's eternity itself—it assumes it from the ten proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : ما ثبت في صفات السموات : أنها غير قابلة للحركة المستقيمة . وكل ما يكون كذلك ، فإنه لا يقبل التفرق والتمزق ، ولا الكون (٢) والفساد . قالت الفلاسفة : فيثبت بهذه الوجوه العشرة : أن العالم أبدي الوجود . وإذا ثبت هذا ، وجب أن يكون أزلياً . لأنه لو لم يكن أزلياً ، لكان معدوماً في الأزل . ولو كان كذلك، كانت حقيقته قابلة للعدم . ولو كان كذلك ، لكانت تلك القابلية باقية أبداً ، وكان يجب صحة العدم عليه بعد وجوده ، ولما كان ذلك محالاً ، ثبت أن حقيقة العالم لا تقبل العدم. وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب كونه أزلياً . فهذا تمام هذا البحث والله أعلم (٣) بالصواب .
The tenth proof: what is established in the attributes of the heavens: that they are not receptive to straight motion. And everything that is so, is not receptive to separation and tearing, nor to generation and corruption. The philosophers said: so it is established by these ten ways that the world is eternal in existence. And if this is established, it must be pre-eternal. Because if it were not pre-eternal, it would have been non-existent in pre-eternity. And if that were so, its essence would be receptive to non-existence. And if that were so, that receptivity would remain forever, and the soundness of non-existence upon it after its existence would be necessary, and since that is impossible, it is established that the essence of the world does not accept non-existence. And if that is so, it must be pre-eternal. This is the end of this investigation, and God knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage contains the tenth proof and the philosophers' concluding inference for the world's pre-eternity. The tenth proof states that the heavens, since they reject straight motion, also reject separation, tearing, generation, and corruption—all of which involve straight motion. Therefore, the heavens are imperishable. The philosophers then conclude from all ten proofs that the world is eternal (abadi al-wujud), i.e., it always exists. They then argue that such eternal existence implies pre-eternity (azali). The reasoning is: if the world were not pre-eternal, it would have been non-existent in the past (al-azal). But then its essence would be capable of non-existence. That capability would persist forever, meaning it could cease to exist after it exists, which is impossible. Therefore, the world's essence cannot accept non-existence, so it must be pre-eternal.

Key Terms
السموات (heavens)
حركة مستقيمة (straight motion)
كون وفساد (generation and corruption)
أبدي (eternal in duration)
أزلي (pre-eternal, without beginning)
عدم (non-existence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Eternal and pre-eternal are the same thing.
Correction: Eternal (abadi) means existing continuously without end; pre-eternal (azali) means existing without beginning. The argument shows that if something is eternal, it must also be pre-eternal, but conceptually they are distinct.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' conclusion, why must the world be pre-eternal if it is eternal?
A) Because anything eternal cannot change
B) Because if it were not pre-eternal, it would be receptive to non-existence, and that would allow it to cease after existing, which is impossible
C) Because pre-eternity is a necessary attribute of perfection
D) Because the world is the effect of a necessary cause

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that eternal existence (abadi) logically entails pre-eternity (azali) because non-pre-eternity would imply a capacity for non-existence, contradicting the world's eternal nature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This argument seems logically sound, yet it leads to a conclusion that contradicts the Islamic belief in a created world. If you were presented with a flawless logical argument that conflicted with your faith, would you have the courage to reject it, or would you be tempted to reinterpret your faith? What does this lesson teach you about the limits of human reason?
?
The philosophers observed the heavens and concluded they are eternal. When you look at the sky, do you see it as a sign of Allah's creative power and intentional beginning, or as a mere natural phenomenon? How can you train yourself to see the universe as a testament to its Creator, the true Pre-Eternal?
?
The argument hinges on the idea that if something had a beginning, it must be capable of ending. Yet as a believer, you affirm that the world will end. Does this challenge your trust in logical proofs? Or does it remind you that ultimate truth comes from revelation, not speculation? What would you say to someone who uses this argument to deny the world's creation?

The Tenth Proof: From Heavenly Bodies to Sempiternity
Razi presents the tenth proof and the philosophers' deductive argument for the world's sempiternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' tenth proof for the eternity of the world and their logical argument that the world must be sempiternal (without beginning).

Core Idea
The world's essential nature makes it impossible for it to begin or end.

Razi here presents the tenth proof, which begins from a property of the heavens. The philosophers then use this to argue that the world is not only eternal in the future but also without a beginning. Their argument is a chain of necessity: if the world had begun, it would always be possible for it to cease, which they deem impossible. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage from Razi and then the English translation to grasp the flow of the argument.
Notice the logical conditional structure.
2
Identify the proof's starting point
Identify the attribute of the heavens that serves as the premise: they do not accept rectilinear motion, and hence no generation/corruption.
3
Trace the philosophers' conclusion
Follow the chain: from the established proofs to the world being eternal (future) to it being sempiternal (past). Understand the conditional argument about possibility of non-existence.
This is the core logical step.
4
Reflect on the impossibility claim
Consider why the philosophers claim it is impossible for the world to cease existing after it exists. Connect to the idea of essential properties.
This is a key point of debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة العاشرة : ما ثبت في صفات السموات : أنها غير قابلة للحركة المستقيمة . وكل ما يكون كذلك ، فإنه لا يقبل التفرق والتمزق ، ولا الكون والفساد . قالت الفلاسفة : فيثبت بهذه الوجوه العشرة : أن العالم أبدي الوجود . وإذا ثبت هذا ، وجب أن يكون أزلياً . لأنه لو لم يكن أزلياً ، لكان معدوماً في الأزل . ولو كان كذلك ، كانت حقيقته قابلة للعدم . ولو كان كذلك ، لكانت تلك القابلية باقية أبداً ، وكان يجب صحة العدم عليه بعد وجوده ، ولما كان ذلك محالاً ، ثبت أن حقيقة العالم لا تقبل العدم. وإذا كان كذلك ، وجب كونه أزلياً . فهذا تمام هذا البحث والله أعلم بالصواب
The tenth proof: What is established regarding the attributes of the heavens: that they are not capable of rectilinear motion. And everything that is like that does not accept division and tearing, nor generation and corruption. The Philosophers said: So by these ten ways it is established that the world is eternal in existence. And if this is established, then it must be sempiternal (azali). Because if it were not sempiternal, it would have been non-existent in pre-eternity (al-azal). And if it were like that, its essence would be receptive to non-existence. And if it were like that, that receptivity would remain forever, and the correctness of non-existence upon it after its existence would be necessary. And since that is impossible, it is established that the essence of the world does not accept non-existence. And if it is like that, then its being sempiternal (azali) is necessary. So this is the end of this research, and God knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth proof for the eternity of the world, followed by the philosophers' reasoning to conclude that the world is eternal (sempiternal). It is a combined proof-and-conclusion passage. The proof begins by stating a property of the heavens: they cannot move in a straight line. From this, it is inferred that heavenly bodies do not undergo division, tearing, generation, or corruption. The philosophers then claim that through these ten proofs (including this one) it is established that the world is eternal in existence (abadī al-wujūd). They then argue that if the world is eternal in existence, it must also be sempiternal (azalī), i.e., without beginning. Their reasoning is a conditional argument: if the world were not sempiternal, it would have been non-existent in pre-eternity (al-azal). In that case, its essence would have the property of being capable of non-existence (qābiliyya li-l-‘adam). That property of being possible to be non-existent would remain forever, because it is an essential characteristic. Therefore, even after the world exists, it would still be possible for it to become non-existent. But they claim that this possibility of ceasing to exist is impossible (muḥāl) for the world, presumably because it is now actual and necessary in some sense. Hence, the premise that the world was non-existent in pre-eternity is false; therefore the world must be sempiternal. The passage concludes the research on this topic with a standard pious phrase: 'And God knows best what is correct.'

Key Terms
أبدي الوجود
أزلي
العدم
القابلية
المحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof for the world's eternity is purely empirical or astrological.
Correction: The argument is logical: it begins from an empirical observation about heavenly motion, but the core reasoning is a conditional argument about essential properties and possibility, not direct observation.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers' argument in this passage, why must the world be sempiternal (azali)?
A) Because it is impossible for the heavens to move rectilinearly.
B) Because if it were not sempiternal, its essence would be receptive to non-existence, and that receptivity would remain forever, making it possible for it to cease existing – which they deem impossible.
C) Because the world is composed of matter and form which cannot be destroyed.
D) Because God's power is limited and cannot create a new world.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that the world's essential nature makes it impossible for it to have a beginning or an end, thus it is sempiternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi ends the passage with 'God knows best what is correct.' After studying this proof, do you feel more convinced of the philosophers' argument or more aware of its limitations? How does the presence of that phrase affect your own certainty about the world's origin?
?
The philosophers argue that the world's essence does not accept non-existence. If you fully internalize the Islamic belief that Allah created the world from nothing, does this argument challenge your trust in Allah's absolute power and freedom? Or does it rather highlight the unique way in which Allah sustains creation? Honestly assess where your heart leans.

The Sixth Proof: Fever Analogy for Eternal Effect
Author uses medical analogy and cites mutakallimun to prove eternal effect from eternal cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fever analogy illustrates that an effect depends on its cause for both its origin and its persistence, thereby supporting the possibility of an eternal effect from an eternal cause.

Core Idea
An effect can persist continuously with its cause, even if both are eternal.

The author presents a medical analogy to show that an effect depends on its cause not only for its beginning but also for its continuation. He then points out that the mutakallimun already accept eternal causation for God's attributes, challenging their denial of an eternal world. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: an analogy followed by a citation of scholarly consensus.
The passage is concise; pay attention to the logical connectors like 'فإن' and 'فكيف'.
2
Understand the fever analogy
Identify the two components: corruption of humors causes fever, and just as fever's occurrence depends on that cause, its persistence also depends on it. This shows that an effect requires its cause continuously.
The analogy is drawn from medicine; it illustrates dependency, not temporal delay.
3
Trace the logical conclusion
The author concludes that attributing a contingent effect to its cause during its persistence is not impossible. This is the key claim: eternal causation can sustain an eternal effect.
4
Consider the appeal to mutakallimun
The author references the mutakallimun's own doctrines: eternal omniscience caused by eternal knowledge, etc. They already accept eternal effects (attributes) caused by eternal causes. So their rejection of an eternal world is inconsistent.
The rhetorical question highlights this inconsistency.
5
Reflect on the misconception
Review the common misunderstanding: some think an eternal effect requires temporal priority. This analogy shows continuity, not temporal order, so that objection fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة: إن عفونة الخلط، توجب حصول الحمى، وكما يفتقر حدوث هذه الحمى إلى حدوث هذا السبب، فكذلك بقاء هذه الحمى، مفتقر إلى بقاء هذا السبب. فإن عند زوال هذه العفونة، يمتنع بقاء الحمى العفونية. فيثبت: أن إسناد الممكن إلى المؤثر حال بقائه: غير ممتنع. وأيضاً: فالمتكلمون يقولون: العالمية الأزلية، معللة بالعلم الأزلي. والقادرية الأزلية معللة بالقدرة الأزلية. والعلم الأزلي، مشروط بالحياة الأزلية. فقد صرحوا بأن الأزلي ممكن أن يكون معللاً بالعلة المؤثرة. فكيف استبعدوا تعليل الأثر القديم، بالمؤثر القديم؟
The sixth proof: That the corruption of the mixture necessitates the occurrence of fever, and just as the occurrence of this fever depends on the occurrence of this cause, so likewise the persistence of this fever depends on the persistence of this cause. For upon the removal of this corruption, the persistence of the fever arising from corruption is impossible. Thus it is established that attributing the contingent to the efficient cause during its permanence is not impossible. Additionally, the mutakallimun say: Eternal omniscience is caused by eternal knowledge, and eternal omnipotence is caused by eternal power, and eternal knowledge is conditioned by eternal life. So they have explicitly stated that the eternal can be caused by the efficient cause. So how have they deemed impossible the causation of the eternal effect by the eternal cause?
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth proof in a series of arguments. It begins with an analogy: just as a fever requires its cause both for its origin and for its continuation (the corruption of bodily humors), so any contingent thing requires its cause both for its coming into existence and for its persistence. If the cause persists, the effect persists; if the cause ceases, the effect ceases. This shows that an effect can be continuously dependent on its cause, even if both are eternal. Then the author appeals to common doctrine among the mutakallimun: they hold that eternal attributes like omniscience and omnipotence are caused by eternal knowledge and power, which are themselves conditioned by eternal life. Thus they already accept that an eternal thing can be caused by another eternal thing. The rhetorical question 'So how have they deemed impossible the causation of the eternal effect by the eternal cause?' highlights an inconsistency in those who deny an eternal effect (such as the world) from an eternal cause (God).

Key Terms

مؤثر
أثر
قديم
متكلمون
علة مؤثرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that an eternal effect requires temporal priority — that cause must precede effect in time.
Correction: The fever analogy shows that an effect can be continuously dependent on its cause without temporal priority; the cause and effect can be co-eternal as long as the dependency is continuous.

Checkpoint
What does the fever analogy in the sixth proof demonstrate?
A) That fever is caused by corruption
B) That an effect can persist as long as its cause persists
C) That all effects are temporal
D) That the mutakallimun reject eternal causation

Key Takeaway
The fever analogy demonstrates that an effect can be continuously dependent on its cause, making an eternal effect from an eternal cause possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Why do you live as if your next breath is guaranteed? The fever analogy shows that your very existence depends on God at every moment, not just at the start. Are you truly aware of that dependency in your daily decisions?
?
The mutakallimun accepted that eternal qualities depend on eternal sources. But in your life, what area of your character or faith have you declared 'self-made'—something you think you maintain without constant divine support? Will you acknowledge Allah's continuous causation in that area today?
?
The author challenges inconsistency. When have you been inconsistent—believing in Allah as Creator but acting as if you own your time, health, or success? What would it mean to live every second as a contingent being, sustained only by His will?
